<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-top: 1px solid #aaa;">Other related appearances</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="hlist" colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/United_States_at_the_1906_Intercalated_Games" title="United States at the 1906 Intercalated Games">1906</a> Intercalated Games</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a></b> was the host nation for the <b><a href="/wiki/2002_Winter_Olympics" title="2002 Winter Olympics">2002 Winter Olympics</a></b> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City,_Utah" title="Salt Lake City, Utah">Salt Lake City, Utah</a>.</p>
<p>These Games were by far the best home Winter Games for the United States, earning 34 total medals, nearly triple their best previous hauls at the <a href="/wiki/1960_Winter_Olympics" title="1960 Winter Olympics">1960 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Squaw_Valley,_Placer_County,_California" title="Squaw Valley, Placer County, California">Squaw Valley, California</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/1932_Winter_Olympics" title="1932 Winter Olympics">1932 Winter Olympics</a> and <a href="/wiki/1980_Winter_Olympics" title="1980 Winter Olympics">1980 Winter Olympics</a>, both in <a href="/wiki/Lake_Placid,_New_York" title="Lake Placid, New York">Lake Placid, New York</a> and the most a host country has won at a single Winter Olympics.</p>
<p>The United States also tied <a href="/wiki/Norway_at_the_1994_Winter_Olympics" title="Norway at the 1994 Winter Olympics">Norway at the 1994 Winter Olympics</a> for most gold medals a host country has won at a Winter Olympics, with 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RecordGolds_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-RecordGolds-1">[1]</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Canada_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics" title="Canada at the 2010 Winter Olympics">Canada</a> broke it during the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RecordGolds_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-RecordGolds-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Olympics were held only months after <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11, 2001</a>. During the opening ceremonies, <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Rogge" title="Jacques Rogge">Jacques Rogge</a>, presiding over his first Olympics as <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">IOC president</a>, told the American athletes that the world was gathered in their country and that their country was overcoming the "horrific tragedy" of that day and stands united with them in promoting the IOC's ideals.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Curling"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Curling_pictogram.svg"><img alt="Curling pictogram.svg" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="30" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Curling_pictogram.svg/30px-Curling_pictogram.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Curling_pictogram.svg/45px-Curling_pictogram.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Curling_pictogram.svg/60px-Curling_pictogram.svg.png 2x" width="30"/></a> Curling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_at_the_2002_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Curling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Curling_at_the_2002_Winter_Olympics" title="Curling at the 2002 Winter Olympics">Curling at the 2002 Winter Olympics</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_tournament">Men's tournament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_at_the_2002_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Men's tournament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Superior CC, <a href="/wiki/Superior,_Wisconsin" title="Superior, Wisconsin">Superior</a></i><br/>
<b>Skip:</b> <a href="/wiki/Tim_Somerville" title="Tim Somerville">Tim Somerville</a><br/>
<b>Third:</b> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Schneeberger&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mike Schneeberger (page does not exist)">Mike Schneeberger</a><br/>
<b>Second:</b> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Myles_Brundidge&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Myles Brundidge (page does not exist)">Myles Brundidge</a><br/>
<b>Lead:</b> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=John_Gordon_(curler)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="John Gordon (curler) (page does not exist)">John Gordon</a><br/>
<b>Alternate:</b> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Donald_Barcombe,_Jr.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Donald Barcombe, Jr. (page does not exist)">Donald Barcombe, Jr.</a></p>

<p><i><a href="/wiki/Bemidji_Curling_Club" title="Bemidji Curling Club">Bemidji CC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bemidji,_Minnesota" title="Bemidji, Minnesota">Bemidji</a></i><br/>
